# schemata-s3

[schemata](https://github.com/matthewdowney/schemata) is a utility for 
abstracting away names and places for file-like data storage by providing 
"context" to naming conventions and IO operations.

schemata-s3 is an S3 context that uses [mcohen01/amazonica](https://github.com/mcohen01/amazonica) 
to enable clojure.java.io utilities like `spit`, `slurp`, `io/reader`, etc. with 
S3 paths.

---

Lein (Uses [Break Versioning](https://github.com/ptaoussanis/encore/blob/master/BREAK-VERSIONING.md)):
```
[org.clojars.mjdowney/schemata-s3 "1.0.0"]
```

---

- [Examples](#examples)
  - [Listing objects](#listing-objects)
  - [Using `slurp` / `spit` with S3 objects](#using-slurp-/-spit-with-s3-objects)
  - [Copying files back & forth](#copying-files-back-&-forth)
- [Naming](#naming)
- [Tests](#tests)

## Examples

Before running the examples you'll need to `require` some stuff and invoke
`s3-context` with some basic configuration (credentials, region, bucket).

Invoking `s3-context` without a naming convention allows us to work with plain 
paths like `s3://my-bucket/path/to/key.log`.

Throughout the examples I'll be working in a REPL session with a bucket I use to
store order book data.

```clojure 
(require '[schemata-s3.core :refer :all])
(require '[schemata.core :as s])

;; Provides IO context for a bucket called "crypto-markets-test"
(def context 
  (s3-context 
     ;; No need to include credentials if AWS CLI 
     ;; is configured locally
    {:endpoint "us-east-1" :access-key "" :secret-key ""}
    "crypto-markets-test"))
; => #'user/context
```

### Listing objects

```clojure 
;; Listing files. The response is a lazy sequence.
(def all-items
  (s/list context))
; => #'user/all-items

(first all-items)
; => "s3://crypto-markets-test/full/Bitstamp_BCH_BTC.2019-04-15.log"

;; Information about listed files
(s/info context (first all-items))
; =>
; {:bucket-name "crypto-markets-test",
;  :etag "26654041db8f64b06c85086cfb0e5b54",
;  :storage-class "STANDARD",
;  :last-modified 1555298405000,
;  :key "full/Bitstamp_BCH_BTC.2019-04-15.log",
;  :size 53879,
;  :base-name "Bitstamp_BCH_BTC.2019-04-15.log"}
```

### Using `slurp` / `spit` with S3 objects
```clojure

(def path 
  "s3://crypto-markets-test/full/Bitstamp_BCH_BTC.2019-04-15.log")
; => #'user/path

(slurp (s/io context path))
```

### Copying files back & forth
Probably more practical than `spit` / `slurp` would be file copying. The 
way to do it with clojure.java.io is:
```clojure
(require '[clojure.java.io :as io])

;; Using the same context & path we used above,
;; we are going to write into the local context.
(let [local-context (s/local-context ".")]
  (with-open [from-s3 (io/reader
                        (s/io context path))
              to-local (io/writer
                         (s/io local-context "downloaded.log"))]
    (io/copy from-s3 to-local)))
; => nil

;; Let's double check that it worked
(slurp "downloaded.log")
; =>

```

But it's such a common task — and one that is often optimizeable given more 
context than just a reader/writer or inputstream/outputstream — there is a `copy` 
utility. 

Let's get rid of our "New Data" line and update the changed log file back to S3.

```clojure 
(def fixed
  (->> (slurp "downloaded.log")
       string/split-lines
       (filter #(not= % "New Data"))
       (string/join "\n")))
; => #'user/fixed

(spit "downloaded.log" fixed)
; => nil

(s/copy 
  "downloaded.log" path  ;; from path, to path
  (s/local-context ".") context) ;; from context, to context
; =>
{:metadata {...},
 :etag "ffa51922ee9970555db5106e195783c7",
 :requester-charged? false,
 :content-md5 "/6UZIu6ZcFVdtRBuGVeDxw=="}

;; ... and let's double check
(slurp (s/io context path))
;=>
```

## Naming

So far we've been working exclusively with providing context to the most general
possible naming convention, the file path. Often our data is structured enough
that we can work with something a little less general.

The path I've been using in the examples is:
```
s3://crypto-markets-test/full/Bitstamp_BCH_BTC.2019-04-15.log
```

Its structure is:
```
s3://BUCKET/TYPE/EXCHANGE_BASE_COUNTER.yyyy-MM-dd.log
```

We get some nice things from defining this structure properly:
```clojure
(def naming-convention
  "This describes a bidirectional relationship between an
  attribute map and the path structure."
  (s/path-convention
    :type
    (s/file-convention
      (s/split-by "_" :exchange :base :counter)
      (s/split-by "." (s/utc :ts "yyyy-MM-dd") "log"))))
; => #'user/naming-convention

(def new-s3-context 
  (s3-context
    {:endpoint "us-east-1"} ;; Credentials too, if necessary
    "crypto-markets-test"
    naming-convention))
; => #'user/new-s3-context

(first (s/list new-s3-context))
=>
{:type "full",
 :exchange "Bitstamp",
 :base "BCH",
 :counter "BTC",
 :ts 1555286400000,
 :schemata-s3.core/info {:bucket-name "crypto-markets-test",
                         :etag "ffa51922ee9970555db5106e195783c7",
                         :storage-class "STANDARD",
                         :last-modified 1555902895000,
                         :key "full/Bitstamp_BCH_BTC.2019-04-15.log",
                         :size 53878,
                         :base-name "Bitstamp_BCH_BTC.2019-04-15.log"}}
```

Now when we list files, we get more than just the path. We get a map of 
attributes that we were previously encoding in the path.

In our `new-s3-context`, we can do everything else in the same terms.

```clojure 
(let [file-spec {:type "full", :exchange "Bitstamp", 
                 :base "BCH", :counter "BTC", :ts 1555286400000}]
```

More about naming conventions on the [schemata core page](https://github.com/matthewdowney/schemata).

## Tests

The core tests for this code are a series of integration tests that copy data
between the local filesystem and S3. In order to run the tests, first create 
a file called `s3-context-test.key` with the contents:
```clojure 
{:bucket "the-bucket-to-use-for-tests"
 :endpoint "us-east-1" ;; Or wherever your bucket is
 ;; No need to include credentials if AWS CLI is configured locally
 :access-key "" 
 :secret-key ""}
```

When run, the tests will operate only inside a `schemata-s3-test` directory inside
of your bucket, so you can share this test bucket with other things. The directory
is created when tests start and removed when tests are done.
 
Run tests with:
```
lein test
```

If you elect to use naming conventions / contexts provided by schemata, you can
leverage `schemata.core/test-with` to perform your own integration tests. See
the schemata core page for more on that.
